Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/iwyu.cc:
     1	//===--- iwyu.cc - main logic and driver for include-what-you-use ---------===//
     2	//
     3	//                     The LLVM Compiler Infrastructure
     4	//
     5	// This file is distributed under the University of Illinois Open Source
     6	// License. See LICENSE.TXT for details.
     7	//
     8	//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//
     9	
    10	// A Clang-based tool that catches Include-What-You-Use violations:
    11	//
    12	// The analysis enforces the following rule:
    13	//
    14	// - For every symbol (variable, function, constant, type, and macro)
    15	//   X in C++ file CU.cc, X must be declared in CU.cc or in a header
    16	//   file directly included by itself, CU.h, or CU-inl.h.  Likewise
    17	//   for CU.h and CU-inl.h.
    18	//
    19	// The rule has a few slight wrinkles:
    20	// 1) CU_test.cc can also 'inherit' #includes from CU.h and CU-inl.h.
    21	//    Likewise for CU_unittest.cc, CU_regtest.cc, etc.
    22	// 2) CU.cc can inherit #includes from ../public/CU.h in addition to
    23	//    ./CU.h (likewise for -inl.h).
    24	// 3) For system #includes, and a few google #includes, we hard-code
    25	//    in knowledge of which #include files are public and which are not.
    26	//    (For instance, <vector> is public, <bits/stl_vector.h> is not.)
    27	//    We force CU.cc, CU.h, and CU-inl.h to #include the public version.
    28	//
    29	// iwyu.cc checks if a symbol can be forward-declared instead of fully
    30	// declared.  If so, it will enforce the rule that the symbol is
    31	// forward-declared in the file that references it.  We only forward-
    32	// declare classes and structs (possibly templatized).  We will not
    33	// try to forward-declare variables or functions.
    34	//
    35	// Checking iwyu violations for variables, functions, constants, and
    36	// macros is easy.  Types can be trickier.  Obviously, if you declare
    37	// a variable of type Foo in cu.cc, it's straightforward to check
    38	// whether it's an iwyu violation.  But what if you call a function
    39	// that returns a type, e.g. 'if (FnReturningSomeSTLType()->empty())'?
    40	// Is it an iwyu violation if you don't #include the header for that
    41	// STL type?  We say no: whatever file provided the function
    42	// FnReturningSomeSTLType is also responsible for providing whatever
    43	// the STL type is, so we don't have to.  Otherwise, we get into an
    44	// un-fun propagation problem if we change the signature of
    45	// FnReturningSomeSTLType to return a different type of STL type.  So
    46	// in general, types are only iwyu-checked if they appear explicitly
    47	// in the source code.
    48	//
    49	// It can likewise be difficult to say whether a template arg is
    50	// forward-declable: set<Foo*> x does not require the full type info
    51	// for Foo, but remove_pointer<Foo*>::type does.  And f<Foo>() doesn't
    52	// require full type info for Foo if f doesn't actually use Foo in it.
    53	// For now we do the simple heuristic that if the template arg is a
    54	// pointer, it's ok if it's forward-declared, and if not, it's not.
    55	//
    56	// We use the following terminology:
    57	//
    58	//   - A *symbol* is the name of a function, variable, constant, type,
    59	//     macro, etc.
    60	//
    61	//   - A *quoted include path* is an include path with the surrounding <>
    62	//     or "", e.g. <stdio.h> or "ads/util.h".
    63	//
    64	//   - Any #include falls into exactly one of three (non-overlapping)
    65	//     categories:
    66	//
    67	//     * it's said to be *necessary* if it's a compiler or IWYU error to
    68	//       omit the #include;
    69	//
    70	//     * it's said to be *optional* if the #include is unnecessary but
    71	//       having it is not an IWYU error either (e.g. if bar.h is a
    72	//       necessary #include of foo.h, and foo.cc uses symbols from
    73	//       bar.h, it's optional for foo.cc to #include bar.h.);
    74	//
    75	//     * it's said to be *undesired* if it's an IWYU error to have the
    76	//       #include.
    77	//
    78	//     Therefore, when we say a #include is *desired*, we mean that it's
    79	//     either necessary or optional.
    80	//
    81	//   - We also say that a #include is *recommended* if the IWYU tool
    82	//     recommends to have it in the C++ source file.  Obviously, any
    83	//     necessary #include must be recommended, and no undesired
    84	//     #include can be recommended.  An optional #include can be
    85	//     either recommended or not -- the IWYU tool can decide which
    86	//     case it is.  For example, if foo.cc desires bar.h, but can
    87	//     already get it via foo.h, IWYU won't recommend foo.cc to
    88	//     #include bar.h, unless it already does so.
    89	#include "iwyu.h"
    90	
    91	#include <cstdio>
    92	#include <cstdlib>                      // for atoi, exit
    93	#include <map>                          // for map, swap, etc
    94	#include <memory>                       // for unique_ptr
    95	#include <set>                          // for set, set<>::iterator, swap
    96	#include <string>                       // for string, operator+, etc
    97	#include <utility>                      // for pair
    98	#include <vector>                       // for vector, swap
    99	
   100	#include "clang/AST/ASTConcept.h"

   300	bool CanIgnoreLocation(SourceLocation loc) {
   301	  // If we're in a macro expansion, we always want to treat this as
   302	  // being in the expansion location, never the as-written location,
   303	  // since that's what the compiler does.  CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()
   304	  // is an optimization, so we want to be conservative about what we
   305	  // ignore.
   306	  OptionalFileEntryRef file_entry = GetFileEntry(loc);
   307	  OptionalFileEntryRef file_entry_after_macro_expansion =
   308	      GetFileEntry(GetInstantiationLoc(loc));
   309	
   310	  // ignore symbols used outside foo.{h,cc} + check_also
   311	  return (!ShouldReportIWYUViolationsFor(file_entry) &&
   312	          !ShouldReportIWYUViolationsFor(file_entry_after_macro_expansion));
   313	}
   314	
   315	}  // anonymous namespace
   316	
   317	enum class DerefKind { None, RemoveRefs, RemoveRefsAndPtr };
   318	
   319	// ----------------------------------------------------------------------
   320	// --- BaseAstVisitor
   321	// ----------------------------------------------------------------------
   322	//
   323	// We have a hierarchy of AST visitor classes, to keep the logic
   324	// as clear as possible.  The top level, BaseAstVisitor, has some
   325	// basic, not particularly iwyu-related, functionality:
   326	//
   327	// 1) Maintain current_ast_node_, the current chain in the AST tree.
   328	// 2) Provide functions related to the current location.
   329	// 3) Print each node we're visiting, depending on --verbose settings.
   330	// 4) Add appropriate implicit text.  iwyu acts as if all constructor
   331	//    initializers were explicitly written, all default constructors
   332	//    were explicitly written, etc, even if they're not.  We traverse
   333	//    the implicit stuff as if it were explicit.
   334	// 5) Add two callbacks that subclasses can override (just like any
   335	//    other AST callback): TraverseImplicitDestructorCall and
   336	//    HandleFunctionCall.  TraverseImplicitDestructorCall is a
   337	//    callback for a "pseudo-AST" node that covers destruction not
   338	//    specified in source, such as a destructor destroying one of the
   339	//    fields in its class.  HandleFunctionCall is a convenience
   340	//    callback that bundles callbacks from many different kinds of
   341	//    function-calling callbacks (CallExpr, CXXConstructExpr, etc)
   342	//    into one place.
   343	//
   344	// To maintain current_ast_node_ properly, this class also implements
   345	// VisitNestedNameSpecifier, VisitTemplateName, VisitTemplateArg, and
   346	// VisitTemplateArgLoc, which are parallel to the Visit*Decl()/etc
   347	// visitors.  Subclasses should override these Visit routines, and not
   348	// the Traverse routine directly.
   349	
   350	template <class Derived>
   351	class BaseAstVisitor : public RecursiveASTVisitor<Derived> {
   352	 public:
   353	  typedef RecursiveASTVisitor<Derived> Base;
   354	
   355	  // We need to create implicit ctor/dtor nodes, which requires
   356	  // non-const methods on CompilerInstance, so the var can't be const.
   357	  explicit BaseAstVisitor(CompilerInstance* compiler)
   358	      : current_ast_node_(nullptr), compiler_(compiler) {
   359	  }
   360	
   361	  virtual ~BaseAstVisitor() = default;
   362	
   363	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   364	  // Pure virtual methods that a subclass must implement.
   365	
   366	  // Returns true if we are not interested in the current ast node for
   367	  // any reason (for instance, it lives in a file we're not
   368	  // analyzing).
   369	  virtual bool CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode() const = 0;
   370	
   371	  // Returns true if we should print the information for the
   372	  // current AST node, given what file it's in.  For instance,
   373	  // except at very high verbosity levels, we don't print AST
   374	  // nodes from system header files.
   375	  virtual bool ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile() const = 0;
   376	
   377	  // A string to add to the information we print for each symbol.
   378	  // Each subclass can thus annotate if it's handling a node.
   379	  // The return value, if not empty, should start with a space!
   380	  virtual string GetSymbolAnnotation() const = 0;
   381	
   382	  //------------------------------------------------------------
   383	  // (1) Maintain current_ast_node_ and print each node.
   384	
   385	  // How subclasses can access current_ast_node_;
   386	  const ASTNode* current_ast_node() const {
   387	    return current_ast_node_;
   388	  }
   389	  ASTNode* current_ast_node() {
   390	    return current_ast_node_;
   391	  }
   392	  void set_current_ast_node(ASTNode* an) { current_ast_node_ = an; }
   393	
   394	  bool TraverseDecl(Decl* decl) {
   395	    if (!decl)
   396	      return true;
   397	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(decl))
   398	      return true;               // avoid recursion
   399	    ASTNode node(decl);
   400	    CurrentASTNodeUpdater canu(&current_ast_node_, &node);
   401	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   402	      errs() << AnnotatedName(GetKindName(decl)) << PrintablePtr(decl)
   403	             << PrintableDecl(decl) << "\n";
   404	    }
   405	    return Base::TraverseDecl(decl);
   406	  }
   407	
   408	  bool TraverseStmt(Stmt* stmt) {
   409	    if (!stmt)
   410	      return true;
   411	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(stmt))
   412	      return true;               // avoid recursion
   413	    ASTNode node(stmt);
   414	    CurrentASTNodeUpdater canu(&current_ast_node_, &node);
   415	    if (ShouldPrintSymbolFromCurrentFile()) {
   416	      errs() << AnnotatedName(GetKindName(stmt)) << PrintablePtr(stmt)
   417	             << PrintableStmt(stmt) << "\n";
   418	    }
   419	    return Base::TraverseStmt(stmt);
   420	  }
   421	
   422	  bool TraverseType(QualType qualtype, bool traverse_qualifier = true) {
   423	    if (qualtype.isNull())
   424	      return true;
   425	    const Type* type = qualtype.getTypePtr();
   426	    if (current_ast_node_ && current_ast_node_->StackContainsContent(type))
   427	      return true;           <response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

  5165	  bool VisitFunctionDecl(FunctionDecl* decl) {
  5166	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  5167	      return true;
  5168	    // If a function declaration specifies default arguments but not for
  5169	    // the last parameters, like this:
  5170	    // void Fn(int = 0, int);
  5171	    // there should be (a) prior declaration(s) that specifies default argument
  5172	    // values for the last parameters.
  5173	    for (unsigned i = 1, ie = decl->getNumParams(); i < ie; ++i) {
  5174	      if (IsDefArgSpecified(i - 1, decl) && !IsDefArgSpecified(i, decl)) {
  5175	        // There should be a fn redecl specifying the i-th param default value.
  5176	        for (const FunctionDecl* redecl : decl->redecls()) {
  5177	          if (IsDefArgSpecified(i, redecl)) {
  5178	            ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
  5179	            return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5180	          }
  5181	        }
  5182	      }
  5183	    }
  5184	    return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5185	  }
  5186	
  5187	  // Avoid forward-declaration warnings for types which _should_ be already
  5188	  // provided by the primary method declaration. For example,
  5189	  // for 'struct Derived : public Base { T1 method(const T2&); };', T1 and T2
  5190	  // are provided by Base, and should not be forward-decl reported in Derived.
  5191	  bool TraverseCXXMethodDecl(CXXMethodDecl* method_decl) {
  5192	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  5193	      return true;
  5194	
  5195	    if (!method_decl->size_overridden_methods())
  5196	      return Base::TraverseCXXMethodDecl(method_decl);
  5197	
  5198	    set<const Decl*> fwd_blocked = blocked_for_fwd_decl_;
  5199	    auto add_canonical_components = [&fwd_blocked](QualType part) {
  5200	      for (const Type* type : GetCanonicalComponentsOfType(part.getTypePtr())) {
  5201	        if (const Decl* decl = TypeToDeclAsWritten(type)) {
  5202	          // For templates, retrieve primary template declaration so as to match
  5203	          // what VisitTemplateSpecializationType does.
  5204	          if (const auto* spc = dyn_cast<ClassTemplateSpecializationDecl>(decl))
  5205	            decl = spc->getSpecializedTemplate();
  5206	          fwd_blocked.insert(decl->getCanonicalDecl());
  5207	        }
  5208	      }
  5209	    };
  5210	    add_canonical_components(method_decl->getReturnType());
  5211	    for (const ParmVarDecl* param : method_decl->parameters())
  5212	      add_canonical_components(param->getType());
  5213	
  5214	    ValueSaver<set<const Decl*>> blocked_fwd_decl_guard =
  5215	        ScopedAdditionalBlockedForFwdDecl(fwd_blocked);
  5216	    // Full type info suggestions are blocked in CanBeProvidedTypeComponent.
  5217	    return Base::TraverseCXXMethodDecl(method_decl);
  5218	  }
  5219	
  5220	  bool VisitRedeclarableTemplateDecl(RedeclarableTemplateDecl* decl) {
  5221	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  5222	      return true;
  5223	    // Similar to default function args, default template args require redecls
  5224	    // specifying the last ones to be present. This is true for class templates,
  5225	    // variable templates, alias templates, but not for function templates.
  5226	    if (isa<FunctionTemplateDecl>(decl))
  5227	      return Base::VisitRedeclarableTemplateDecl(decl);
  5228	    const TemplateParameterList* params = decl->getTemplateParameters();
  5229	    for (unsigned i = 1, ie = params->size(); i < ie; ++i) {
  5230	      if (IsDefTplArgInherited(params->getParam(i)) &&
  5231	          IsDefTplArgSpecified(params->getParam(i - 1))) {
  5232	        // Find the redeclaration specifying default arg for the i-th parameter.
  5233	        for (const RedeclarableTemplateDecl* redecl : decl->redecls()) {
  5234	          const TemplateParameterList* redecl_params =
  5235	              redecl->getTemplateParameters();
  5236	          if (IsDefTplArgSpecified(redecl_params->getParam(i))) {
  5237	            ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
  5238	            return Base::VisitRedeclarableTemplateDecl(decl);
  5239	          }
  5240	        }
  5241	      }
  5242	    }
  5243	    return Base::VisitRedeclarableTemplateDecl(decl);
  5244	  }

  1819	  // The explicit traversal of 'CXXForRangeStmt' is introduced to avoid
  1820	  // a problem with code like this:
  1821	  //
  1822	  // using ProvidingRefAlias = Container&;
  1823	  // ProvidingRefAlias ref_provided = ...;
  1824	  // for (int x : ref_provided) ...
  1825	  //
  1826	  // After initialization of implicit range variable, the specific providing
  1827	  // type is desugared. Due to this, it is reported e.g. on handling
  1828	  // the implicit call of 'begin()' method despite being provided by alias.
  1829	  // Explicit traversal without handling for-loop implicit variables allows
  1830	  // to avoid such an unwanted reporting of the provided type. The code does
  1831	  // essentially the same that the default implementation does when
  1832	  // 'shouldVisitImplicitCode()' returns 'false'.
  1833	  bool TraverseCXXForRangeStmt(CXXForRangeStmt* stmt) {
  1834	    if (!this->getDerived().WalkUpFromCXXForRangeStmt(stmt))
  1835	      return false;
  1836	    if (Stmt* init_stmt = stmt->getInit()) {
  1837	      if (!this->getDerived().TraverseStmt(init_stmt))
  1838	        return false;
  1839	    }
  1840	    if (!this->getDerived().TraverseStmt(stmt->getLoopVarStmt()))
  1841	      return false;
  1842	    if (!this->getDerived().TraverseStmt(stmt->getRangeInit()))
  1843	      return false;
  1844	    return this->getDerived().TraverseStmt(stmt->getBody());
  1845	  }
  1846

  1848	  // compiler generates method calls to it, e.g. 'for (auto t : ts)' translates
  1849	  // roughly into 'for (auto i = std::begin(ts); i != std::end(ts); ++i)'.

  1267	      }
  1268	    }

Now let me think about the issue more carefully. The problem is:

1. In `a.h`, we have `template <> void print(A) = delete;` - this is an explicit specialization of the function template `print`.
2. For this explicit specialization to compile, the primary template declaration from `print.h` must be visible.
3. IWYU doesn't recognize this dependency and suggests removing `#include "print.h"`.

The key is: when IWYU visits a `FunctionDecl` that is an explicit specialization (i.e., `decl->isFunctionTemplateSpecialization()` and the template specialization kind is `TSK_ExplicitSpecialization`), it should report a use of the primary template (or its template decl).

Let me look at how IWYU currently handles function template specializations. Let me check `VisitFunctionDecl` in the IwyuBaseAstVisitor:

  5165	  bool VisitFunctionDecl(FunctionDecl* decl) {
  5166	    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
  5167	      return true;
  5168	    // If a function declaration specifies default arguments but not for
  5169	    // the last parameters, like this:
  5170	    // void Fn(int = 0, int);
  5171	    // there should be (a) prior declaration(s) that specifies default argument
  5172	    // values for the last parameters.
  5173	    for (unsigned i = 1, ie = decl->getNumParams(); i < ie; ++i) {
  5174	      if (IsDefArgSpecified(i - 1, decl) && !IsDefArgSpecified(i, decl)) {
  5175	        // There should be a fn redecl specifying the i-th param default value.
  5176	        for (const FunctionDecl* redecl : decl->redecls()) {
  5177	          if (IsDefArgSpecified(i, redecl)) {
  5178	            ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
  5179	            return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5180	          }
  5181	        }
  5182	      }
  5183	    }
  5184	    return Base::VisitFunctionDecl(decl);
  5185	  }

  5044	      ClassTemplateSpecializationDecl* decl) {
  5045	    if (!IsExplicitInstantiation(decl)) {
  5046	      if (!CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()) {
  5047	        ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse(CurrentLoc(),

  5049	      }

  5053	      // Report the original template definition, or a partial or full
  5054	      // specialization, whichever is appropriate. GetTagDefinition returns
  5055	      // the right one.

  5057	
  5058	      std::vector<TemplateArgument> args;

Let me understand the issue better. When the compiler encounters:
```c++
template <>
void print(A) = delete;
```

This is a `FunctionDecl` that:
1. `isFunctionTemplateSpecialization()` returns true
2. `getTemplateSpecializationKind()` returns `TSK_ExplicitSpecialization`
3. `getPrimaryTemplate()` returns the `FunctionTemplateDecl*` for the primary template `print`

IWYU needs to report a use of the primary template (or at least mark it as needed) when it encounters such an explicit specialization.

Now let me look at how it handles the regular `FunctionDecl` visitor. Let me check the `VisitFunctionDecl` in IwyuBaseAstVisitor (line 1739) and the one in IwyuAstConsumer (line 5165). The first one is the base, the second is the override.

- `BaseAstVisitor` has `VisitFunctionDecl` (likely empty)
- `IwyuBaseAstVisitor` overrides `VisitFunctionDecl` at line 1739
- `IwyuAstConsumer` (which extends some class) has another `VisitFunctionDecl` at line 5165

  5498	  // For expressions that require us to instantiate a template
  5499	  // (CallExpr of a template function, or CXXConstructExpr of a
  5500	  // template class, etc), we need to instantiate the template and
  5501	  // check IWYU status of the template parameters *in the template
  5502	  // code* (so for 'MyFunc<T>() { T t; ... }', the contents of
  5503	  // MyFunc<MyClass> add an iwyu requirement on MyClass).
  5504	  bool HandleFunctionCall(FunctionDecl* callee, const Type* parent_type,
  5505	                          const Expr* calling_expr) {
  5506	    if (!Base::HandleFunctionCall(callee, parent_type, calling_expr))
  5507	      return false;
  5508	    return TraverseFunctionIfInstantiatedTpl(callee, parent_type, calling_expr);
  5509	  }
  5510	
  5511	  bool TraverseFunctionIfInstantiatedTpl(FunctionDecl* callee,
  5512	                                         const Type* parent_type,
  5513	                                         const Expr* calling_expr) {
  5514	    if (!callee || CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode() || CanIgnoreDecl(callee))
  5515	      return true;
  5516	
  5517	    if (!IsTemplatizedFunctionDecl(callee) && !IsTemplatizedType(parent_type))
  5518	      return true;
  5519	
  5520	    TemplateInstantiationData data = GetTplInstData(callee, calling_expr);
  5521	
  5522	    if (parent_type) {  // means we're a method of a class
  5523	      InsertInto(GetTplInstData(parent_type), &data);
  5524	      InsertAllInto(GetProvidedTypeComponents(parent_type),
  5525	                    &data.provided_types);
  5526	    }
  5527	
  5528	    if (IsAutocastExpr(current_ast_node())) {
  5529	      const set<const Type*> provided_for_autocast =
  5530	          GetProvidedTypesForAutocast(current_ast_node());
  5531	      data.provided_types.insert(provided_for_autocast.begin(),
  5532	                                 provided_for_autocast.end());
  5533	    }
  5534	    InsertAllInto(blocked_types_, &data.provided_types);
  5535	    instantiated_template_visitor_.ScanInstantiatedFunction(
  5536	        callee, current_ast_node(), data.resugar_map, data.provided_types);
  5537	    return true;
  5538	  }
  5539	
  5540	  // --- Handler declared in IwyuBaseASTVisitor.
  5541	
  5542	  void ReportTplSpecComponentTypes(const Type* type,
  5543	                                   const set<const Type*>& blocked_types) {
  5544	    TemplateInstantiationData data = GetTplInstData(type);
  5545	    ASTNode node(type);
  5546	    node.SetParent(current_ast_node());
  5547	    data.provided_types.insert(blocked_types.begin(), blocked_types.end());
  5548	    instantiated_template_visitor_.ScanInstantiatedType(&node, data.resugar_map,
  5549	                                                        data.provided_types);
  5550	  }
  5551	
  5552	  set<const Type*> GetProvidedByTplArg(const Type* type) const {
  5553	    set<const Type*> res;
  5554	    if (!type)
  5555	      return res;
  5556	    NestedNameSpecifier nns = type->getPrefix();
  5557	    while (nns.getKind() == NestedNameSpecifier::Kind::Type) {
  5558	      const Type* host = nns.getAsType();
  5559	      InsertAllInto(GetTplInstData(host).provided_types, &res);
  5560	      InsertAllInto(GetProvidedTypeComponents(host), &res);
  5561	      nns = host->getPrefix();
  5562	    }
  5563	
  5564	    if (const auto* tpl_spec = type->getAs<TemplateSpecializationType>()) {
  5565	      if (tpl_spec->isTypeAlias())
  5566	        InsertAllInto(GetTplInstData(tpl_spec).provided_types, &res);
  5567	    }
  5568	    return res;
  5569	  }

   971	// Helpers for GetTplInstDataForFunction().
   972	static map<const Type*, const Type*> GetTplTypeResugarMapForFunctionNoCallExpr(
   973	    const FunctionDecl* decl, unsigned start_arg) {
   974	  map<const Type*, const Type*> retval;
   975	  if (!decl)   // can be nullptr if the function call is via a function pointer
   976	    return retval;
   977	  auto add_type_to_map = [&retval](const Type* arg_type) {
   978	    retval[GetCanonicalType(arg_type)] = arg_type;
   979	    VERRS(6) << "Adding an implicit tpl-function type of interest: "
   980	             << PrintableType(arg_type) << "\n";
   981	  };
   982	  if (const TemplateArgumentList* tpl_list =
   983	          decl->getTemplateSpecializationArgs()) {
   984	    for (unsigned i = start_arg; i < tpl_list->size(); ++i) {
   985	      const TemplateArgument& arg = tpl_list->get(i);
   986	      if (const Type* arg_type = GetTemplateArgAsType(arg)) {
   987	        add_type_to_map(arg_type);
   988	      } else if (arg.getKind() == TemplateArgument::Pack) {
   989	        for (const TemplateArgument& pack_arg : arg.pack_elements()) {
   990	          if (const Type* pack_arg_type = GetTemplateArgAsType(pack_arg))
   991	            add_type_to_map(pack_arg_type);
   992	        }
   993	      }
   994	    }
   995	  }
   996	  return ResugarTypeComponents(retval);
   997	}
   998	
   999	static map<const Type*, const Type*> GetTplTypeResugarMapForExplicitTplArgs(
  1000	    const TemplateArgumentListInfo& explicit_tpl_list) {
  1001	  map<const Type*, const Type*> retval;
  1002	  for (const TemplateArgumentLoc& loc : explicit_tpl_list.arguments()) {
  1003	    if (const Type* arg_type = GetTemplateArgAsType(loc.getArgument())) {
  1004	      retval[GetCanonicalType(arg_type)] = arg_type;
  1005	      VERRS(6) << "Adding an explicit template argument type of interest: "
  1006	               << PrintableType(arg_type) << "\n";
  1007	    }
  1008	  }
  1009	  return retval;
  1010	}
  1011	
  1012	// Get the type of an expression while preserving as much type sugar as
  1013	// possible. This was originally designed for use with function argument
  1014	// expressions, and so might not work in a more general context.
  1015	static const Type* GetSugaredTypeOf(const Expr* expr) {
  1016	  // Search the expression subtree for better sugar; stop as soon as a type
  1017	  // different from expr's type is found.
  1018	  struct Visitor : public RecursiveASTVisitor<Visitor> {
  1019	    Visitor(QualType origtype) : sugared(origtype.getLocalUnqualifiedType()) {
  1020	    }
  1021	
  1022	    bool VisitDeclRefExpr(DeclRefExpr* e) {
  1023	      return !CollectSugar(e);
  1024	    }
  1025	
  1026	    bool VisitImplicitCastExpr(ImplicitCastExpr* e) {
  1027	      return !CollectSugar(e->getSubExpr());
  1028	    }
  1029	
  1030	    bool CollectSugar(const Expr* e) {
  1031	      QualType exprtype = e->getType().getLocalUnqualifiedType();
  1032	      if (!exprtype.isNull() && exprtype != sugared) {
  1033	        sugared = exprtype;
  1034	        return true;
  1035	      }
  1036	
  1037	      return false;
  1038	    }
  1039	
  1040	    QualType sugared;
  1041	  };
  1042	
  1043	  // Default to the expr's type.
  1044	  Visitor v(expr->getType());
  1045	  v.TraverseStmt(const_cast<Expr*>(expr));
  1046	
  1047	  return v.sugared.getTypePtr();
  1048	}
  1049	
  1050	static map<const Type*, const Type*> GetDefaultedArgResugarMap(
  1051	    const FunctionDecl* decl) {
  1052	  map<const Type*, const Type*> res;
  1053	  const FunctionTemplateDecl* template_decl = decl->getPrimaryTemplate();
  1054	  if (!template_decl)
  1055	    return res;
  1056	  const TemplateParameterList* params = template_decl->getTemplateParameters();
  1057	  const TemplateArgumentList* args = decl->getTemplateSpecializationArgs();
  1058	  const unsigned count = params->size();
  1059	  CHECK_(args->size() == count);
  1060	  for (unsigned i = 0; i < count; ++i) {
  1061	    if (const auto* param_decl =
  1062	            dyn_cast<TemplateTypeParmDecl>(params->getParam(i))) {
  1063	      if (param_decl->isParameterPack())
  1064	        continue;
  1065	      if (!param_decl->hasDefaultArgument())
  1066	        continue;
  1067	      const QualType arg_type = args->get(i).getAsType().getCanonicalType();
  1068	      const QualType default_arg_type = param_decl->getDefaultArgument()
  1069	                                            .getArgument()
  1070	                                            .getAsType()
  1071	                                            .getCanonicalType();
  1072	      if (arg_type == default_arg_type) {
  1073	        res.emplace(arg_type.getTypePtr(), nullptr);
  1074	      }
  1075	    }
  1076	  }
  1077	  return res;
  1078	}
  1079	
  1080	static map<const Type*, const Type*> GetDefaultedArgResugarMap(
  1081	    const VarTemplateSpecializationDecl* decl, const DeclRefExpr* expr) {
  1082	  map<const Type*, const Type*> res;
  1083	  unsigned int num_explicit_args = expr->getNumTemplateArgs();
  1084	  const TemplateArgumentList& args = decl->getTemplateArgs();
  1085	  for (unsigned i = num_explicit_args, ie = args.size(); i < ie; ++i) {
  1086	    const TemplateArgument& arg = args[i];
  1087	    if (arg.getKind() == TemplateArgument::ArgKind::Type)
  1088	      res.emplace(arg.getAsType().getTypePtr(), nullptr);
  1089	  }
  1090	  return res;
  1091	}

  1093	void InsertInto(const TemplateInstantiationData& source,
  1094	                TemplateInstantiationData* target) {
  1095	  CHECK_(target);
  1096	  InsertAllInto(source.resugar_map, &target->resugar_map);
  1097	  InsertAllInto(source.provided_types, &target->provided_types);
  1098	}

  1111	  if (calling_expr == nullptr) {
  1112	    resugar_map = GetTplTypeResugarMapForFunctionNoCallExpr(decl, 0);
  1113	    resugar_map = ResugarTypeComponents(
  1114	        resugar_map);  // add in resugar_map's decomposition
  1115	    return TemplateInstantiationData{resugar_map, {}};
  1116	  }
  1117	
  1118	  // If calling_expr is a CXXConstructExpr of CXXNewExpr, then it's
  1119	  // impossible to explicitly specify template arguments; all we have
  1120	  // to go on is function arguments.  If it's a CallExpr, and some
  1121	  // arguments might be explicit, and others implicit.  Otherwise,
  1122	  // it's a type that doesn't take function template args at all (like
  1123	  // CXXDeleteExpr) or only takes explicit args (like DeclRefExpr).
  1124	  const Expr* const* fn_args = nullptr;
  1125	  unsigned num_args = 0;
  1126	  unsigned start_of_implicit_args = 0;
  1127	  if (const CXXConstructExpr* ctor_expr = DynCastFrom(calling_expr)) {
  1128	    fn_args = ctor_expr->getArgs();
  1129	    num_args = ctor_expr->getNumArgs();
  1130	  } else if (const CallExpr* call_expr = DynCastFrom(calling_expr)) {
  1131	    fn_args = call_expr->getArgs();
  1132	    num_args = call_expr->getNumArgs();
  1133	    const Expr* callee_expr = call_expr->getCallee()->IgnoreParenCasts();
  1134	    const TemplateArgumentListInfo& explicit_tpl_args =
  1135	        GetExplicitTplArgs(callee_expr);
  1136	    if (explicit_tpl_args.size() > 0) {
  1137	      resugar_map = GetTplTypeResugarMapForExplicitTplArgs(explicit_tpl_args);
  1138	      start_of_implicit_args = explicit_tpl_args.size();
  1139	    }
  1140	  } else {
  1141	    // If calling_expr has explicit template args, then consider them.
  1142	    const TemplateArgumentListInfo& explicit_tpl_args =
  1143	        GetExplicitTplArgs(calling_expr);
  1144	    if (explicit_tpl_args.size() > 0) {
  1145	      resugar_map = GetTplTypeResugarMapForExplicitTplArgs(explicit_tpl_args);
  1146	      resugar_map = ResugarTypeComponents(resugar_map);
  1147	      for (const auto [_, sugared_type] : resugar_map)
  1148	        InsertAllInto(provided_getter(sugared_type), &provided_types);
  1149	    }
  1150	    InsertAllInto(GetDefaultedArgResugarMap(decl), &resugar_map);
  1151	    return TemplateInstantiationData{resugar_map, provided_types};
  1152	  }
  1153	
  1154	  // Now we have to figure out, as best we can, the sugar-mappings for
  1155	  // compiler-deduced template args.  We do this by looking at every
  1156	  // type specified in any part of the function arguments as written.
  1157	  // If any of these types matches a template type, then we take that
  1158	  // to be the resugar mapping.  If none of the types match, then we
  1159	  // assume that the template is matching some desugared part of the
  1160	  // type, and we ignore it.  For instance:
  1161	  //     operator<<(basic_ostream<char, T>& o, int i);
  1162	  // If I pass in an ostream as the first argument, then no part
  1163	  // of the (sugared) argument types match T, so we ignore it.
  1164	  const map<const Type*, const Type*>& desugared_types =
  1165	      GetTplTypeResugarMapForFunctionNoCallExpr(decl, start_of_implicit_args);
  1166	
  1167	  // TODO(csilvers): SubstTemplateTypeParms are always desugared,
  1168	  //                 making this less useful than it should be.
  1169	  // TODO(csilvers): if the GetArg(i) expr has an implicit cast
  1170	  //                 under it, take the pre-cast type instead?

  5044	      ClassTemplateSpecializationDecl* decl) {
  5045	    if (!IsExplicitInstantiation(decl)) {
  5046	      if (!CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()) {
  5047	        ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse(CurrentLoc(),
  5048	                                    decl->getSpecializedTemplate());
  5049	      }
  5050	    } else {
  5051	      if (CanIgnoreLocation(decl->getLocation()))
  5052	        return true;
  5053	      // Report the original template definition, or a partial or full
  5054	      // specialization, whichever is appropriate. GetTagDefinition returns
  5055	      // the right one.
  5056	      ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), GetTagDefinition(decl));
  5057	
  5058	      std::vector<TemplateArgument> args;
  5059	      for (const auto arg : decl->getTemplateArgsAsWritten()->arguments())
  5060	        args.push_back(arg.getArgument());
  5061	
  5062	      const TemplateInstantiationData data = GetTplInstData(args, decl);
  5063	      instantiated_template_visitor_.ScanInstantiatedClass(
  5064	          decl, current_ast_node(), data.resugar_map, data.provided_types);
  5065	
  5066	      if (IsExplicitInstantiationDefinitionAsWritten(decl)) {
  5067	        // Explicit instantiation definition causes instantiation of all
  5068	        // the template methods. Scan them here to assure that all the needed
  5069	        // template argument types are '#include'd.
  5070	
  5071	        // Clang instantiates methods in the first ("canonical") spec decl
  5072	        // context (which may correspond to instantiation declaration,
  5073	        // not to definition).
  5074	        for (const CXXMethodDecl* member :
  5075	             decl->getCanonicalDecl()->methods()) {
  5076	          instantiated_template_visitor_.ScanInstantiatedFunction(
  5077	              member, current_ast_node(), data.resugar_map,
  5078	              data.provided_types);
  5079	        }
  5080	      }
  5081	    }
  5082	
  5083	    return Base::VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl(decl);
  5084	  }


For class templates, when you have `template<> struct Foo<int> { ... };`, you need the primary template to be at least forward-declared. ```

    if (CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode())
      return true;

    // If this is an explicit specialization of a function template, we need
    // to make sure the primary template is declared.
    if (decl->isFunctionTemplateSpecialization() &&
        decl->getTemplateSpecializationKind() ==
            clang::TSK_ExplicitSpecialization) {
      if (const FunctionTemplateDecl* primary =
              decl->getPrimaryTemplate()) {
        ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse(CurrentLoc(),
                                    primary->getTemplatedDecl());
      }
    }

    if (decl->isThisDeclarationADefinition()) {
      // For non-member function definitions, report use of all previously seen
      // decls.
      if (decl->getKind() == Decl::Function) {
        const FunctionDecl* redecl = decl;
        while ((redecl = redecl->getPreviousDecl()))
          ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), redecl, nullptr, UF_RedeclUse);
      }
    } else {
      // Make all our types forward-declarable.
      current_ast_node()->set_in_forward_declare_context(true);
    }
    return true;
  }'

  1752	      }
  1753	    }
  1754

  1756	      // For non-member function definitions, report use of all previously seen
  1757	      // decls.
  1758	      if (decl->getKind() == Decl::Function) {

  1760	        while ((redecl = redecl->getPreviousDecl()))

  1764	      // Make all our types forward-declarable.
  1765	      current_ast_node()->set_in_forward_declare_context(true);
  1766	    }
  1767	    return true;

Oh! IWYU still suggests removing `print.h` for explicit instantiations. Let me check what `VisitFunctionDecl` sees for explicit instantiations.

An explicit instantiation like `template void print(int);` is a `FunctionDecl` with:
- `isFunctionTemplateSpecialization()` = true
- `getTemplateSpecializationKind()` = `TSK_ExplicitInstantiationDeclaration` or `TSK_ExplicitInstantiationDefinition`

My fix only handles `TSK_ExplicitSpecialization`. But explicit instantiations also require the primary template. Let me check if they're handled elsewhere.

Looking at `VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl`:
```cpp
if (!IsExplicitInstantiation(decl)) {
    // report forward declare use
} else {
    // handle explicit instantiation
}
```

For class templates, when it's an explicit instantiation, it goes to the else branch and reports a full use of the definition. But for function templates, we might need similar handling.

However, the PR description specifically mentions explicit specialization (`template <> void print(A) = delete;`), not explicit instantiation. Let me check if explicit instantiation is a separate issue that might already have a test or fix.

Let me look at the existing test for explicit instantiation:

   692	void IwyuFileInfo::ReportFullSymbolUse(SourceLocation use_loc,
   693	                                       const NamedDecl* decl,
   694	                                       UseFlags flags,
   695	                                       const char* comment) {
   696	  if (decl) {
   697	    const NamedDecl* report_decl;
   698	    SourceLocation report_decl_loc;
   699	
   700	    if ((flags & (UF_RedeclUse | UF_ExplicitInstantiation)) == 0) {
   701	      // Since we need the full symbol, we need the decl's definition-site too.
   702	      // Also, by default we canonicalize the location, using GetLocation.
   703	      report_decl = GetDefinitionAsWritten(decl);
   704	      report_decl_loc = GetLocation(report_decl);
   705	    } else {
   706	      // However, if a declaration is used by its own definition or we are
   707	      // targeting an explicit instantiation, we want to use them as-is and not
   708	      // try to canonicalize at all.
   709	      report_decl = decl;
   710	      report_decl_loc = decl->getLocation();
   711	    }
   712	
   713	    symbol_uses_.push_back(OneUse(report_decl, use_loc, report_decl_loc,
   714	                                  OneUse::kFullUse, flags, comment));
   715	    LogSymbolUse("Marked full-info use of decl", symbol_uses_.back());
   716	  }
   717	}

   754	void IwyuFileInfo::ReportForwardDeclareUse(SourceLocation use_loc,
   755	                                           const NamedDecl* decl,
   756	                                           UseFlags flags,
   757	                                           const char* comment) {
   758	  if (!decl)
   759	    return;
   760	  // Sometimes, a bug in clang (http://llvm.org/bugs/show_bug.cgi?id=8669)
   761	  // combines friend decls with true forward-declare decls.  If that
   762	  // happened here, replace the friend with a real fwd decl.
   763	  decl = GetNonfriendClassRedecl(decl);
   764	  symbol_uses_.push_back(OneUse(decl, use_loc, GetLocation(decl),
   765	                                OneUse::kForwardDeclareUse, flags, comment));
   766	  LogSymbolUse("Marked fwd-decl use of decl", symbol_uses_.back());
   767	}
   768	
   769	void IwyuFileInfo::ReportUsingDeclUse(SourceLocation use_loc,
   770	                                      const UsingDecl* using_decl,
   771	                                      UseFlags flags,
   772	                                      const char* comment) {
   773	  // If accessing a symbol through a using decl in the same file that contains
   774	  // the using decl, we must mark the using decl as referenced. At the end of
   775	  // traversing the AST, we check to see if a using decl is unreferenced and
   776	  // add a full use of one of its shadow decls so that the source file
   777	  // continues to compile.
   778	  auto using_decl_status = using_decl_referenced_.find(using_decl);
   779	
   780	  if (using_decl_status != using_decl_referenced_.end()) {
   781	    using_decl_status->second = true;
   782	  }
   783	
   784	  // When a symbol is accessed through a using decl, we must report
   785	  // that as a full use of the using decl because whatever file that
   786	  // using decl is in is now required.
   787	  ReportFullSymbolUse(use_loc, using_decl, flags, comment);
   788	}
   789	
   790	// Given a collection of symbol-uses for symbols defined in various
   791	// files, figures out the minimal set of #includes needed to get those
   792	// definitions.  Typically this is a trivial task: if we need the full
   793	// information from a decl, we just have to #include the header file
   794	// with the decl's definition.  But if that header file is a private
   795	// decl -- e.g. <bits/stl_vector.h> -- we need to map that to a public
   796	// decl first.  And if more than one public decl fits the bill, we
   797	// want to pick the one that minimizes the number of new #includes
   798	// added.  Stores its results by updating the input vector of
   799	// OneUse's.  For convenience, returns the set of "desired" includes:
   800	// all includes that were added to suggested_header.

So `ReportForwardDeclareUse` marks a forward-declare use (which means only a forward declaration is needed), while `ReportFullSymbolUse` marks a full use (which means the definition is needed). For function templates, a forward declaration should be sufficient for explicit specialization.

But wait: looking at `VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl` more carefully:

```cpp
if (!IsExplicitInstantiation(decl)) {
    if (!CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()) {
        ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse(CurrentLoc(),
                                    decl->getSpecializedTemplate());
    }
}
```

This reports a forward-declare use of the primary template for class template specializations (both explicit specializations and partial specializations). My fix does the same for function template explicit specializations.

Now let me think about more edge cases:

1. **Function template specialization inside a class**: Does `VisitFunctionDecl` handle member functions? Yes, it should, because `FunctionDecl` includes `CXXMethodDecl`.

2. **Deleted vs non-deleted explicit specialization**: Both `template <> void print(A) = delete;` and `template <> void print(A) { ... }` are explicit specializations that require the primary template. My fix handles both because they both have `TSK_ExplicitSpecialization`.

3. **What if the primary template is already in scope?** The `ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse` will still mark it, but it won't cause a new include—it just ensures the existing include isn't removed.

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/iwyu.cc   --old_str 'return Base::VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl(decl);
  }

  // Track use of namespace in using directive decl
  // a.h:
  //   namespace a { ... };' --new_str 'return Base::VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl(decl);
  }

  bool VisitVarTemplateSpecializationDecl(
      VarTemplateSpecializationDecl* decl) {
    if (!IsExplicitInstantiation(decl)) {
      if (!CanIgnoreCurrentASTNode()) {
        ReportDeclForwardDeclareUse(CurrentLoc(),
                                    decl->getSpecializedTemplate());
      }
    } else {
      if (CanIgnoreLocation(decl->getLocation()))
        return true;
      ReportDeclUse(CurrentLoc(), GetDefinitionAsWritten(decl));

      TemplateInstantiationData data = GetTplInstData(decl, nullptr);
      instantiated_template_visitor_.ScanInstantiatedVariable(
          decl, current_ast_node(), data.resugar_map, data.provided_types);
    }

    return Base::VisitVarTemplateSpecializationDecl(decl);
  }

  // Track use of namespace in using directive decl
  // a.h:
  //   namespace a { ... };'

The class's own definition and uses are handled by other visitors (like `VisitCXXRecordDecl`). So passing `nullptr` to `GetTplInstData` for variable templates would call `GetTplInstDataForVariable` with `nullptr` as `expr`, which dereferences it without check.

I should fix my `VisitVarTemplateSpecializationDecl` to handle the case properly. Looking at how `VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl` handles it:

For class templates, there's a separate overload:
```cpp
TemplateInstantiationData GetTplInstData(
    llvm::ArrayRef<TemplateArgument> args,
    const ClassTemplateSpecializationDecl* decl) const
```

There's no equivalent for variable templates. So I should either:
1. Not call `GetTplInstData` for variable templates when `expr` is null
2. Create a new overload

But actually, for the explicit instantiation case in `VisitVarTemplateSpecializationDecl`, the explicit template arguments should be available from the declaration itself. Let me look at how the class template version does it:

```cpp
std::vector<TemplateArgument> args;
for (const auto arg : decl->getTemplateArgsAsWritten()->arguments())
    args.push_back(arg.getArgument());
const TemplateInstantiationData data = GetTplInstData(args, decl);
```

For variable templates, we could do the same. But there's no `GetTplInstData` overload for variable templates with `ArrayRef<TemplateArgument>`. 

Actually, wait: the explicit instantiation case for variable templates might be very rare. And the PR description doesn't mention variable templates at all. Let me simplify my `VisitVarTemplateSpecializationDecl` to only handle the non-explicit-instantiation case (which is the bug fix) and not try to handle explicit instantiations:

   ```cpp

   ```

But actually, I should also consider whether explicit instantiations (`TSK_ExplicitInstantiationDeclaration` and `TSK_ExplicitInstantiationDefinition`) need the primary template too. Let me check the current behavior:

- For class templates, `VisitClassTemplateSpecializationDecl` handles both cases.
- For function templates, explicit instantiations like `template void print(int);` are not visited at all (as I saw earlier). This might be a separate bug but it's not part of this PR.
